тАШ рдЕрдпрдорд┐рд╣ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╡рд╛рдорджреЗрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдорд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдпрдореН ред рдЖрджреНрдпрд╛ рдЬрдЧрддреА рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН –’ рдЕрдпрдорд┐рд╣рд╛рджреМ рдЬрдЧрддреА рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ ред рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдкреНрд░рдгрдпрдиреЗ тАШрдЕрдпрдорд┐рд╣ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрддреН ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдореН - ’ рдЕрдпрдорд┐рд╣ рдкреНрд░рдердореЛ рдзрд╛рдпрд┐ рдзрд╛рддреГрднрд┐рд░рд┐рддрд┐ рддреБ рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреНрдпрд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрдпреЛрд░рд╛рджреНрдпреЗ’ (рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. реи. резрен) рдЗрддрд┐ ред

Jamison Brereton

7 (303)
Agni
V─Бmadeva Gautama
11 verses: jagat─л 1, anuс╣гс╣нubh 2тАУ6, triс╣гс╣нubh 7тАУ11
Although this hymn consists of verses in three different meters, it was clearly con ceived as a unity, as was already seen by Oldenberg (1888: 153). The hymn begins, as often, with the ritual installation of the current sacrificial fire, which is set against the backdrop of the primal installation of Agni, treated in verses 1тАУ5, in a non insistent ring structure. Verses 6 and 7, though in different meters, express the cen tral mysteries of Agni and therefore define a sort of omphalos. Verse 6 is structured as a series of paradoxes concerning the nature of fire. Verse 7, quite reminiscent of the omphalos verse IV.5.7, refers to the elements of the sacrifice in riddling fashion. The hymn then turns to AgniтАЩs role as messenger between Earth and Heaven (vss. 8тАУ9, 11, first mentioned in vs. 3), with some vivid metaphorical description of fireтАЩs appearance and its consuming of flammable тАЬfoodтАЭ (vss. 9тАУ11).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Agni Intro.: The published introduction. states that AgniтАЩs role as messenger is first mentioned in vs. 3; this should be corrected to vs. 4.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis invoker of the gods and minister of frequent worship, who is to be glorified at sacrifices, has been plural ced first (of the gods) by the performers of the rite; the Agni whom Apnav─Бna and other Bhс╣Ыgus lighted in the woods for the sake of all men, marvellous (in his acts), and soverign (over all).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This one has been installed here first by the installers, as best sacrificing Hotar, to be reverently invoked in the ceremonies,
whom Apnav─Бna and the Bhr╠еgus made to shine, brilliant in the woods, extending to every clan.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Apnav─Бna appears with the Bhс╣Ыgus also in VIII.102.4, but nothing more is known of him (cf. Mayr., Personenname s.v.). Scarlatta (366-67), though without disc., renders it not as a sg. PN, but as a nom. pl. adj. modifying the Bhс╣Ыgus (тАЬdie reichen (?) Bhс╣ЫgusтАЭ), presumably to a stem *├бpnavan-, roughly parallel to ├бpnasvant-.

However, the usage in VIII.102.4 makes it clear that at least in that passage it is a PN. In c viruruc├║с╕е gives a bad cadence, and by meaning it could easily belong to the redupl. aor. ar┼лruca-. The same p─Бda-final sequence (save for accent) тАж bhс╣Ы╠Бgavo v├н rurucuс╕е is also found at X.122.5. It is therefore tempting (see Oldenberg [Noten], Arnold [Ved. Metre 128] for the temptation) to lengthen the reduplicating vowel. However, the undeniable 3rd pl. pf. ending (aor. should be *r┼лrucan) and the existence of other transitive exx. of rurucuс╕е in other metrical positions (see K├╝mmel 431) temper the temptation. Still, IтАЩd be inclined to read *vir┼лrucuс╕е and assume that the stem has been secondarily incorporated into the pf. For further disc. see comm. ad IV.16.4.

HERE by ordainers was this God appointed first Invoker, best at worship, to be praised at rites:
Whom Apnavana, and the Bhrgus caused to shine bright-coloured in the wood, spreading from home to home.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen, Agni, is the light of you, bright-shining, to be manifested; for therefore have mortals accepted you as to be worshipped among mankind.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni, when will there be manifestation of you, the god, in the regular order?
For it was therefore that the mortals seized you as the one to be reverently invoked in the clansтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The point of the abrupt question opening this vs. must be that mortals have established Agni in his ritual role (vs. 1, 2cd), but Agni is not reliably fulfilling this role by manifesting himself at the proper times.

Griffith

When shall thy glory as a God, Agni, be suddenly shown forth.
For mortal men have held thee fast, adorable in all their homes,

Oldenberg

Agni! When will the splendour of thee, the god, appear in the right way? For verily the mortals have seized thee who shouldst be magnified in the houses.

Geldner

Agni! Wann wird deine, des Gottes, Erscheinung wie sich’s geb├╝hrt stattfinden? Denn darum haben dich die Sterblichen festgehalten als den in den Clanen zu berufenden Priester.

Grassmann

Wann wurde nach der Ordnung dir, o Agni, Gottes-Herrlichkeit? Da war’s, als in die H├дuser dich, die Menschen setzten als den Preis.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬContemplating you in every dwelling, truthful intelligent, (brilliant with sparks) like the sky with stars, the perfecter of all sacrifices.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(The mortals) looking at (you,) truthful and discriminating (/widely observable) like heaven with its stars,
(you) who create laughter [=fireтАЩs crackling] for all ceremonies in every house,

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. continues the syntactic frame of vs. 2, with the nom. pl. subj.

(тАЬmortalsтАЭ of 2d) modified by the pres. part. p├б┼Ыyantaс╕е and Agni in the acc. sg.

v├нcetasam in p─Бda a is a pun, playing on the standard ambiguity of the root тИЪcit, which means both тАШperceiveтАЩ and тАШappearтАЩ. Referring to AgniтАЩs mental qualities, adjacent to с╣Ыt─Б╠Бv─Бnam тАШtruthfulтАЩ, it means тАШdiscriminatingтАЩ, but the simile in b, тАЬlike heaven with its stars,тАЭ actualizes the тАШappearтАЩ sense.

The тАЬlaughterтАЭ of Agni is the merry crackling of the fire.

Griffith

Seeing thee faithful to the Law, most sapient, like the starry heaven,
Illumining with cheerful ray each solemn rite in every house.

Oldenberg

Seeing the righteous, wise one, like the heaven with the stars, who produces joy at all sacrifices, from house to houseтАФ

Geldner

Den Rechttuenden, Umsichtigen erkennend wie den Himmel an den Sternen, den Erheller aller Opfer in jedem Hause,

Grassmann

Da sie den reinen gl├дnzen sahn dem sterngeschm├╝ckten Himmel gleich, Ihn, der die Gottesdienste all’ in jedem Hause sch├╢ner macht.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMen have brought, for the sake of all people, the swift messenger of the worshipper (to the gods), who (rules) over all mankind, the manifester, the resplendent.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Messenger of the worshipper: d┼лtam vivasvataс╕е: vivasvataс╕е = manuс╣гyasya yajama~nasya, of the man, of the worshipper; the replendent: bhс╣Ыgav─Бс╣Зam bhс╣Ыguvad ─Бcarantam, going like Bhс╣Ыgu, i.e., d─лpyam─Бnam ityartha, shining, or being kindled

Jamison Brereton

(You,) the swift messenger of Vivasvant, who sur(mount) all the domains,
the ─Аyus brought (you) here as beacon, associated with the Bhr╠еgus, for every clan.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. also appears to continue the syntax of vs. 3, with another acc. phrase referring to Agni (p─Бda a), though given the 3rd pl. verb in c (─Б╠Бjabhruс╕е) that could govern the acc., the vs. can be syntactically self-contained.

Griffith

Vivasvan’s envoy living men have taken as their ensign, swift,
The ruler over all mankind, moving like Bhrgu in each home.

Oldenberg

The quick messenger of Vivasvat who rules over all human tribes: Him the ├Вyus have brought hither to every house, the light, him who belongs to the Bhrigus.

Geldner

Den flinken Boten des Vivasvat, der ├╝ber alle V├╢lker herrscht, ihn den Bhrigugenossen brachten die Ayus├╢hne als Wahrzeichen zu jedem Clane.

Grassmann

Vivasvats schnellen Boten ihn, der alles Lebende beherrscht, Als Leuchte nahm die Menschheit ihn, der funkelt hell in jedem Haus.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHim, abiding in the maternal (waters) and in the woods, loved, yet unapproached, wonderful, hidden in a cave, endowed with knowledge, seeking (oblations) from any quarter.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Loved yet unapproached: v─лtam k─Бntam: a┼Ыritam, d─Бhabhaya+dasevitam, bright or beloved, not honoured or served, through fear of being burnt; seeking oblations from any quarter: k┼лcidarthinam: i.e., kvacit, anywhere, anyhow; seeking fuel, butter: samid─Бjy─Бdi haviс╕е sv─лkurvantam

Jamison Brereton

Him, enveloped in mothers who are ever new, enveloped in wood (yet) unfixed,
set in hiding though brilliant, easily found but aiming who
knows where.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is structured as a series of paradoxes, one per p─Бda. The least clear is in p─Бda a, since there is only one qualifier, the loc. ┼Ы├б┼Ыvat─лс╣гu m─Бtс╣Ы╠Бс╣гu тАЬin ever new mothers,тАЭ which must be construed with v─лt├бm тАШenvelopedтАЩ in b. The paradox there is that ordinarily one has only one mother and that mother is not self-renewing. The physical reference must be to the pieces of wood (his mothers) in which fire inheres and from which he flashes out one by one. This physical image is developed in b: the fire is within wood – therefore apparently in a fixed place – but is unfixed, in that it is in constant motion in and over the sticks of wood. In c the fire inherent in the wood, therefore hidden, is also bright when it catches. Note another instance of the root тИЪcit, citr├бm (matching the same word in 1d). And finally in d, when the fire catches itтАЩs easy to see and therefore to find, but its movements are unpredictable.

06-07 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

Though vs. 6 belongs metrically and syntactically with what precedes – it is in Anuс╣гс╣нubh like vss. 2-5 and the accusative descriptive phrases hang off vs. 5 – it belongs thematically with vs. 7, as noted in the published introduction. Both vss. treat the mystery of the ritual fire, and being at the center of the hymn, they form a sort of omphalos.

Griffith

In his Eternal Mothers, in the wood, concealed and unapproached,
Kept secret though his flames are bright seekingon all sides, quickly found.

Oldenberg

Him who is enveloped in many mothers, in the wood 1, who does not rest thereon (?) 2, who is brilliant, though hidden in secret, easily to be found, and striving for all that is desired.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhom, when they desist from slumber, the devout propitiate in the abode of water at every sacrifice; the mighty Agni, to whom oblations are to be offered with reverence, who truthful always, accepts the sacrifice.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When, at the separation of the grain [=spreading of the ritual grass?], at the same udder [=the sacrifice?], on the domain of truth [=the ritual ground?], the gods take pleasure,
great Agni, on whom the oblation is bestowed with reverence, the truthful one, is always pursuing (his missions) for the ceremony.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs., particularly the first p─Бda, has been subjected to a variety of interpretations, which I will not pursue in detail here. The vs. is reminiscent of, though far less difficult than, IV.5.7, and in both cases I think it concerns the ritual and the layout of the ritual ground. The loc. phrase sas├бsya тАж v├нyut─Б тАЬat the separation of the grainтАЭ I take as a reference to the spreading of the barhis, the ritual grass; it seems to correspond to the loc. phrase in IV.5.7c sas├бsya c├бrman тАЬon the hide of the grain.тАЭ See also V.21.4, where Agni is urged to sit тАЬon the womb of grainтАЭ (sas├бsya y├│nim). тАЬAt the same udderтАЭ (s├бsminn ┼л╠Бdhan) is also found in nearby IV.10.8, also with apparent reference to the sacrifice or the ritual ground.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On 3rd sg. veс╕е (тИЪv─л) in 7d, see comm. ad II.5.3. Here the form serves as a pivot, veс╕е in 8a having the more morphologically orthodox 2nd ps. reference. The near identity of the two adjacent phrases, 7d #v├йr adhvar─Б╠Бya and 8a #v├йr adhvar├бsya (d┼лty─Б╠Аni), requires us to consider them together. The first is clearly 3rd sg. (with nom. agn├нс╕е in the preceding p─Бda, nom. с╣Ыt─Б╠Бv─Б in the same p─Бda). The 2nd ps. ref. of the second only emerges in p─Бda 8c, with 2nd sg. verb ─лyase. The poet seems to want first to enforce the 3rd ps. reference of the verb (even in 8ab the nom. pf. participles vidv─Б╠Бn and cikitv─Б╠Бn appear to continue the 3rd ps.) and then require us to construct a paradigm: 2nd sg. v├йs [sandhi v├йr], 3rd sg. v├йs [sandhi v├йr], like 2nd sg. (─Б╠Б)var, 3rd sg.

(─Б╠Б)var, which I invoked ad II.5.3 to explain the anomalous 3rd sg. v├йs. We can see this sequence as a variant on poetic repair.

The near repetition of the VP in 8a also clarifies the construction of the verb in 7d, with gapped object. I take dat. adhvar─Б╠Бya (7d) and gen. adhvar├бsya (8a) as filling essentially the same functional role.

06-07 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

Though vs. 6 belongs metrically and syntactically with what precedes – it is in Anuс╣гс╣нubh like vss. 2-5 and the accusative descriptive phrases hang off vs. 5 – it belongs thematically with vs. 7, as noted in the published introduction. Both vss. treat the mystery of the ritual fire, and being at the center of the hymn, they form a sort of omphalos.

Griffith

That as food spreads forth in this earthly udder, Gods may rejoice them in the home of Order,
Great Agni, served with reverence and oblation, flies ever to the sacrifice, the Faithful.

Oldenberg

When the gods rejoiced in the тАж of the herbs 1, in that udder 2, in the foundation of Rita 3, the great -Agni, to whom offerings are made with adoration, the righteous one, always approached eagerly for the sake of sacrifice.

Geldner

Wenn sich die G├╢tter beim Entleeren der Nahrung am gleichen Euter, am Ursprungsort der Wahrheit erg├╢tzen, dann m├╢ge der gro├Яe Agni, dem unter Verneigung Spenden dargebracht werden, f├╝r die Opferhandlung Sorge tragen, der jederzeit das Rechte tut.

Grassmann

Wenn hier am Euter dieses Kraut’s die G├╢tter im heil’gen Sitze hier und dort sich laben, So geht ans Opfer stets der grosse Agni, versehn mit Tr├дnken, ehrfurchtsvoll, der heil’ge.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou who are all-knowing understand the functions of a messenger (of the gods) at the sacrifice; well informed of both heaven and earth and the intermediate (firmament), and a most intelligent, ancient, and amplifying envoy, you go up the ascents of heaven.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, as the knowing one, pursue your missions for the ceremony between the two world-halves, observing them both together.
You speed as the messenger chosen from of old, since you know better the means of ascending to heaven.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The VP тИЪvid ─Бr├│dhanaс╣Г div├бс╕е (a variant of our vid├║с╣гс╣нaro div├б ─Бr├│dhan─Бni) occurs in the next hymn, IV.8.2, 4, assuring that the acc. here is governed by the comparative to the pf. part. vid├║с╣гс╣нara-. With most (though not Grassmann, Witzel Got┼Н) I take ─Бr├│dhana- as belonging with тИЪruh тАШclimbтАЩ (/тИЪrudh тАШgrowтАЩ), not тИЪrudh тАШobstructтАЩ. On the difficulties in sorting out these roots, see EWA s.v. RODH2 .

Jamison Brereton Notes

On 3rd sg. veс╕е (тИЪv─л) in 7d, see comm. ad II.5.3. Here the form serves as a pivot, veс╕е in 8a having the more morphologically orthodox 2nd ps. reference. The near identity of the two adjacent phrases, 7d #v├йr adhvar─Б╠Бya and 8a #v├йr adhvar├бsya (d┼лty─Б╠Аni), requires us to consider them together. The first is clearly 3rd sg. (with nom. agn├нс╕е in the preceding p─Бda, nom. с╣Ыt─Б╠Бv─Б in the same p─Бda). The 2nd ps. ref. of the second only emerges in p─Бda 8c, with 2nd sg. verb ─лyase. The poet seems to want first to enforce the 3rd ps. reference of the verb (even in 8ab the nom. pf. participles vidv─Б╠Бn and cikitv─Б╠Бn appear to continue the 3rd ps.) and then require us to construct a paradigm: 2nd sg. v├йs [sandhi v├йr], 3rd sg. v├йs [sandhi v├йr], like 2nd sg. (─Б╠Б)var, 3rd sg.

(─Б╠Б)var, which I invoked ad II.5.3 to explain the anomalous 3rd sg. v├йs. We can see this sequence as a variant on poetic repair.

The near repetition of the VP in 8a also clarifies the construction of the verb in 7d, with gapped object. I take dat. adhvar─Б╠Бya (7d) and gen. adhvar├бsya (8a) as filling essentially the same functional role.

Griffith

Bird of each rite, skilled in an envoy’s duties, knowing both worlds and that which lies between them,
Thou goest from of old a willing Herald, knowing full well heaven’s innermost recesses.

Oldenberg

1 Thou, the knowing one, hast eagerly performed the messengership of the sacrifice, looking over both ends, over the two worlds. Thou goest as a messenger, chosen from of old, thou who knowest best the ascents to heaven.

Grassmann

Er geht, auf Opfers Botschaft sich verstehend, hin zwischen beiden Welten, wohl sie kennend; Erw├дhlt als Bote, wanderst du von jeher, des Himmels Heiligthum aufs beste kennend.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDark is the path of you wo are bright; the light is before you; your moving radiance is the chief of (all luminous) bodies; when the present (worshippers) take up the germ (in the sticks of attrition) you are speedily genitive rated, and become indeed the messenger (of the sacrifice).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Black is your course, (though) you are gleaming; your light is in front. The flickering beam of your (various) wondrous forms is single
when (your mothers, though) not impregnated, conceive an embryo, and you, even immediately at birth, become a messenger.

Jamison Brereton Notes

My interpr. of this vs. differs from the standard ones in several ways. First, in b most tr. take v├бpuс╣г─Бm ├нd ├йkam as a nominal sentence: тАЬ(this is) one of the wonders.тАЭ In contrast, I take b as describing the moment of the birth of the ritual fire: a single physical flame rising from the wood, though it is well known that Agni has many forms (v├бp┼лс╣Гс╣гi e.g., III.1.8, 18.5, 55.9). Thus, ├йkam modifies arc├нс╕е, and the p─Бda is a single clause.

P─Бdas bc then sketch a double paradox: the beam of the just-born Agni is single, though he has many forms and though a number of mothers conceive him as an embryo (d├бdhate ha g├бrbham). P─Бda c also contains another paradox: his mothers conceive him though they are unimpregnated (├бprav─лt─Б[с╕е]). My interpr. depends on reading pl. ├бprav─лt─Бс╕е contra the Pp, which has singular -─Б – followed by Grassmann and by all the standard tr., which also then must take d├бdhate as a thematic 3rd sg. (or perhaps a short-vowel subjunctive). With Oldenberg (Noten), I take d├бdhate as the expected indic. 3rd plural mid. to the redupl. pres. to тИЪdh─Б and ├бprav─лt─Б as representing ├бprav─лt─Бс╕е in sandhi. The same form, in the pl., is found in the very similar passage III.55.5 ant├бrvat─лс╕е suvate ├бprav─лt─Б(с╕е), which also describes AgniтАЩs тАЬvirgin birthтАЭ: тАЬHaving (him) within, (though) unimpregnated they give birth to (him).тАЭ AgniтАЩs multiple mothers also figure earlier in our own hymn, 6a.

The published translation takes p─Бda d as a subordinate clause, still under the control of y├бd beginning p─Бda c, primarily because of the accent on bh├бvasi. However, it is quite possible that d is a separate main clause (тАЬimmediately at birth, you become a messengerтАЭ) with the verbal accent owing to the immediately following ├нd. Many of the exx. given by Grassmann (no. 5, s.v. ├нd) of accented verbs followed by ├нd are p─Бda-initial and therefore non-probative (since they would be accented anyway), but there is a sturdy residue of non-initial apparent main clause verbs with accent.

Griffith

Bright God, thy path is black: light is before thee: thy moving splendour is the chief of wonders.
When she, yet unimpregnate, hath conceived thee, even when newly born thou art an envoy.

Oldenberg

Thy path is black. Light is before thee, the red one. Thy flame is speedy. This is one of the wonders: when the virgin conceives (thee as her) child 1, thou becomest a messenger, as soon as thou art born.

Geldner

Schwarz ist dein Weg, w├дhrend du hell bist; vor dir ist heller Schein, wandelnd deine Flamme - eines der Wunder! Das andere ist, da├Я die Mutter unbelegt die Leibesfrucht empf├дngt und du geboren sofort Bote wirst.

Grassmann

Dein Weg ist hell, voran geht Glanz dem Hellen, und flatternd Licht ist der Gestalten eine; Kaum hat die Jungfrau ihren Sohn geboren, so bist du gleich nach der Geburt schon Bote.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe light of the speedily-genitive rated is visible, and when the win fans the flame, he (Agni) spreads his blazing tongue among the trees, and with his (glowing) teeth consumes the standing (fuel, his) food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Immediately at birth, his strength comes to light, when the wind fans his flame.
He twists his sharp tongue into the thickets. Even hard foods he fragments with his jaws.

Jamison Brereton Notes

An undeniable ex. of a predicated perfect part., d├бdс╣Ы┼Ы─Бnam.

On the supposed separate root тИЪdi тАШdestroyтАЩ, see comm. ad III.34.1.

Griffith

Yet newly born, his vigour is apparent when the wind blows upon his fiery splendour,
His sharpened tongue he layeth on the brushwood, and with his teeth e’en solid food consumeth.

Oldenberg

As soon as he is born, his strength shows itself, when the wind blows upon his flame. He turns his sharp tongue among the dry brushwood. Even solid food he tears to pieces with his teeth.

Geldner

Sogleich, wenn er geboren ist, zeigt sich seine Kraft, wenn der Wind hinter seiner Flamme dreinbl├дst. Er ringelt seine spitze Zunge im d├╝rren Holze; auch die festen Speisen zerteilt er mit den Z├дhnen.

Grassmann

Im kaum gebornen zeiget sich die Kraft schon, wenn seinem Licht der Windhauch blasend nachweht; Er streckt die spitze Zunge in das Buschwerk, zermalmt mit Z├дhnen auch die harten Speisen.

Elizarenkova

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рдпрддреН рдпрдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рддреГрд╖реБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдореЗрд╡ рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛ рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд╛рд╖реНрдард╛рджреАрдирд┐ рддреГрд╖реБрдгрд╛ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░реЗрдг рд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рд╕рдореВрд╣реЗрди рд╡рд╡рдХреНрд╖ рд╡рд╣рддрд┐ ред рджрд╣рддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдпрд╣реНрд╡рдГ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреН рд╕рдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рддреГрд╖реБрдореН рдЖрддреНрдорд╛рдирдВ рджреВрддрдВ рдХреГрдгреБрддреЗ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирджреВрддрдВ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ ред рдирд┐рдЬреВрд░реНрд╡рдиреН рдХрд╛рд╖реНрдард╛рдирд┐ рдирд┐рдГрд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдг рджрд╣рдиреНрдирдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд╡рд╛рддрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛рдпреЛрдГ рдореЗрд│рд┐рдВ рдмрд▓рдВ рд╕рдЪрддреЗ рд╕реЗрд╡рддреЗ ред рдЖрд╢реБрдВ рди ред рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╕рд╛рджреА рдпрдерд╛рд╢реНрд╡рдВ рддрдерд╛ рдЕрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдЧрдордирд╢реАрд▓реЛрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЬрдпрддреЗ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд┐рдирдВ рдмрд▓рд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ ред рд╣рд┐рдиреНрд╡реЗ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдпрддрд┐ рдЪ рее рее рен рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen quickly, with rapid (radiance), he has carried off his food, the mighty Agni makes (himself) the fleet messenger (of the worshipper); consuming (the fuel), he allies himself with the force of the wind, and as (a horseman) urges his fast steed, so the rapid going Agni, invigorates and urges (his flames).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When thirstily he has grown with (his flame) thirsting for food, he makes the thirsty (flame) into his messengerтАФyouthfully
exuberant Agni.
He accompanies the roaring of the wind as he grinds down (the bush); he incites it like a swift (horse); the steed is impelled.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Rather than supplying a verb to govern ├бnn─Б (e.g., Geldner тАЬdie Speisen (verzehrend)тАЭ), I allow tс╣Ыс╣г├║с╣З─Б тАШthirsting (for)тАЩ to govern the acc. In b the standard tr. supply тАШwindтАЩ: тАЬhe makes the thirsty (wind) his messenger.тАЭ I resist this because it is Agni who is always the messenger (e.g., in this hymn 4a, 8a, 8c, 9d), and so I think it more likely that in this case Agni is making some part of himself (flame) into that messenger. A small problem is the masc.

gender of tс╣Ыс╣г├║m: the words for тАШflame, blazeтАЩ in this hymn are neut. (arc├нs- 9b, ┼Ыoc├нs5c, 10b). However, a word like m. ┼Ы├│ka- is always available, or we could attribute the masc. of tс╣Ыс╣г├║m to attraction to d┼лt├бm or even take it as the modifier of d┼лt├бm (тАЬhe makes [his flame] into a thirsty messengerтАЭ).

Griffith

When he hath borne off food with swift flame swiftly, strong Agni makes himself a speedy envoy,
Follows the rustling of the wind, consuming, and courser-like, speeds, drives the swift horse onward.

Oldenberg

When he thirstily has grown strong by thirsty food 1, restless Agni appoints a thirsty messenger. Consuming (the wood) he follows the тАж 2 of the wind. He seems to drive forward a quick horse; the racer speeds along.

Geldner

Wenn er gierig die Speisen verzehrend mit der gierigen Flamme w├дchst, so macht der j├╝ngste Agni den gierigen Wind zu seinem Boten. Er folgt verzehrend dem Rauschen des Windes, er spornt gleichsam seinen Renner an, das Rennpferd wird zur Eile getrieben.

Grassmann

Voll Gier nach Speisen wachsend durch den gier’gen, macht Agni schnell ihn sich zum gier’gen Boten; Verzehrend folgt er nach des Windes Brausen; beeilt den schnellen, treibt ihn vor, der Renner.

Elizarenkova

╨Ъ╨╛╨│╨┤╨░ ╨╢╨░╨┤╨╜╨╛ (╨┐╨╛╨╢╨╕╤А╨░╤П) ╨┐╨╕╤Й╤Г, ╨╛╨╜ ╨▓╤Л╤А╨╛╤Б ╤Б╨╛ (╤Б╨▓╨╛╨╕╨╝) ╨╢╨░╨┤╨╜╤Л╨╝ (╨┐╨╗╨░╨╝╨╡╨╜╨╡╨╝),
╨о╨╜╤Л╨╣ ╨Р╨│╨╜╨╕ ╨┤╨╡╨╗╨░╨╡╤В ╨▓╨╡╤Б╤В╨╜╨╕╨║╨╛╨╝ ╨╢╨░╨┤╨╜╤Л╨╣ ╨▓╨╡╤В╨╡╤А.
╨б╨╢╨╕╨│╨░╤П (╨▓╤Б╨╡), ╨╛╨╜ ╤Б╨╗╨╡╨┤╤Г╨╡╤В ╨╖╨░ ╤И╤Г╨╝╨╛╨╝ ╨▓╨╡╤В╤А╨░.
╨Ю╨╜ ╤Б╨╗╨╛╨▓╨╜╨╛ ╨┐╤А╨╕╤И╨┐╨╛╤А╨╕╨▓╨░╨╡╤В ╨▒╤Л╤Б╤В╤А╨╛╨│╨╛ (╨║╨╛╨╜╤П), ╤Б╨║╨░╨║╤Г╨╜╨░ ╨┐╨╛╨│╨╛╨╜╤П╤О╤В.

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)
  • рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ
  • рд╡рд╛рдорджреЗрд╡реЛ рдЧреМрддрдордГ
  • рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН
  • рдзреИрд╡рддрдГ
рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкрд┐ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! (рдпрддреН) рдЬреЛ (рдпрд╣реНрд╡рдГ) рдмреЬреЗ (рдЕрд░реНрд╡рд╛) рдШреЛреЬреЗ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ (рдирд┐рдЬреВрд░реНрд╡рдиреН) рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рд╢реАрдШреНрд░ рдЪрд▓рддреА рд╣реБрдИ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА (рддреГрд╖реБрдгрд╛) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рддрд╛ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛) рдЕрдиреНрди рдЖрджрд┐рдХ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рддреГрд╖реБ) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░ (рд╡рд╡рдХреНрд╖) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рд╛рддреА рд╣реИ (рддреГрд╖реБрдореН) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдХрд╛рд░реА (рджреВрддрдореН) рд╕рдорд╛рдЪрд╛рд░ рдкрд╣реБрдБрдЪрд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЬрди рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд╛рдк рдХреЛ (рдХреГрдгреБрддреЗ) рдХрд░рддреА рд╣реИ рдФрд░ (рд╡рд╛рддрд╕реНрдп) рдкрд╡рди рдХреЗ (рдореЗрд│рд┐рдореН) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдо рдХрд╛ (рд╕рдЪрддреЗ) рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдз рдХрд░рддреА рд╣реИ рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЬрди (рдЖрд╢реБрдореН) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░ рдЪрд▓рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдШреЛреЬреЗ рдХреЗ (рди) рд╕рджреГрд╢ (рд╡рд╛рдЬрдпрддреЗ) рдЪрд▓рд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдореИрдВ (рд╣рд┐рдиреНрд╡реЗ) рдЪрд▓рд╛рдКрдБ, рдЙрд╕рдХреЛ рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ рдЬрд╛рдирд┐рдпреЗ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА рдФрд░ рд╡рд╛рдпреБ рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреЗ рдпреЛрдЧ рдХреА рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдХреЛ рдЬрд╛рдиреЗрдВ рддреЛ рд╡реЗ рджреВрдд рдФрд░ рдШреЛреЬреЗ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рджреВрд░ рд╡рд╛рд╣рди рдФрд░ рд╕рдорд╛рдЪрд╛рд░ рдХреЛ рдкрд╣реБрдБрдЪрд╛ рд╕рдХреЗрдВ реерезрезрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕ рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реерезрезрее рдпрд╣ рд╕рд╛рддрд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рд╕рд╛рддрд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпрджреНрдпреЛ рдпрд╣реНрд╡реЛрд╜рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╡ рдирд┐рдЬреВрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрдирдЧреНрдирд┐рд╕реНрддреГрд╖реБрдгрд╛рд╜рдиреНрдирд╛ рддреГрд╖реБ рд╡рд╡рдХреНрд╖ рддреГрд╖реБ рджреВрддрдорд┐рд╡ рдХреГрдгреБрддреЗ рд╡рд╛рддрд╕реНрдп рдореЗрд│рд┐рдВ рд╕рдЪрддреЗ рдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рд╢реБрдВ рди рд╡рд╛рдЬрдпрддреЗрд╜рд╣рдВ рд╣рд┐рдиреНрд╡реЗ рддрдВ рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдиреАрдд реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрди рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкрд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддреГрд╖реБ) рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдореНред рддреГрд╖реНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежреи.резрел) (рдпрддреН) рдпрдГ (рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛) рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛рджреАрдирд┐ (рддреГрд╖реБрдгрд╛) рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░реЗрдг (рд╡рд╡рдХреНрд╖) рд╡рд╣рддрд┐ (рддреГрд╖реБрдореН) рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгрдореН (рджреВрддрдореН) рджреВрддрдорд┐рд╡ (рдХреГрдгреБрддреЗ) рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ (рдпрд╣реНрд╡рдГ) рдорд╣рд╛рдиреН (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрддреН (рд╡рд╛рддрд╕реНрдп) (рдореЗрд│рд┐рдореН) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдордореН (рд╕рдЪрддреЗ) рд╕рдорд╡реИрддрд┐ (рдирд┐рдЬреВрд░реНрд╡рдиреН) рдирд┐рддрд░рд╛рдВ рд╕рджреНрдпреЛ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН (рдЖрд╢реБрдореН) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдЧрд╛рдорд┐рдирдорд╢реНрд╡рдореН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рд╡рд╛рдЬрдпрддреЗ) рдЧрдордпрддрд┐ (рд╣рд┐рдиреНрд╡реЗ) рдЧрдордпреЗрдп (рдЕрд░реНрд╡рд╛) рд╡рд╛рдЬреАрд╡ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрджрд┐ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджреНрд╡рд╛рдпреНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдпреЛрдЧрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдЬрд╛рдиреАрдпреБрд╕реНрддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рддреЗ рджреВрддрд╡рджрд╢реНрд╡рд╡рджреНрджреВрд░рдВ рдпрд╛рдирдВ рд╕рдорд╛рдЪрд╛рд░рдВ рдЪ рдЧрдордпрд┐рддреБрдВ рд╢рдХреНрдиреБрдпреБрдГ реерезрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ реерезрезрее рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдкреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрдореЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреА рдорд╛рдгрд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрдд рд╡ рд╡рд╛рдпреВ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреАрдВрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдпреЛрдЧрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдЬрд╛рдгрддрд╛рдд рддреЗрд╡реНрд╣рд╛ рддреА рджреВрддрд╛рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рд╡ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рджреВрд░ рдпрд╛рди рд╡ рд╡рд╛рд░реНрддрд╛ рдкреЛрдЪрд╡реВ рд╢рдХрддрд╛рдд. рее резрез рее
